xxxvii.
A Psalm of David,
A a 1 (k) Fret not thyself because of evildoers, neither be thou envious against the workers of
iniquity. 2 For they shall soon be cut down like the grass, and wither as the green herb.
3 (l) Trust in the Lord, and do good; so shalt thou dwell in the land, and verily thou shalt
be fed. 4 Delight thyself also in the Lord ; and he shall give thee the desires of thine heart.
5 (j) Commit thy way unto the Lord ; trust also in him ; and he shall bring it to pass. 6 And
he shall bring forth thy righteousness as the light, and thy judgment as the noonday.
7 (t) Best in the Lord, and wait patiently for him : fret not thyself because of him who
prospereth in his way, because of the man who bringeth wicked devices to pass. 8 (it) Cease
from anger, and forsake wrath : fret not thyself in any wise to do evil. 9 For evildoers shall
be cut off: but those that wait upon the Lord, they shall inherit the earth. 10 (l) For yet
a little while, and the wicked shall not be : yea, thou shalt diligently consider his place, and
it shall not he. 11 But the meek shall inherit the earth ; and shall delight themselves in the
abundance of peace.
bl 2 (>) The wicked plotteth against the just, and gnasheth upon him with his teeth. 13 The
Lord shall laugh at him : for he seeth that his day is coming. 14 (n) The wicked have
drawn out the sword, and have bent their bow, to cast down the poor and needy, and to slay
such as be of upright conversation. 15 Their sword shall enter into their own heart,
and their bows shall be broken.
B 16 (id) A little that a righteous man hath is better than the riches of many wicked.

Psalm xxxvii. is acrostic: but it differs from some others in having four lines (two couplets) assigned
to each letter, except 1 (v. 7), 2 (r. 20), and p (v. 34), which each have three lines (or a triplet).
Further, these three letters occur in remarkable places:—the first, T, is the seventh verse from the
beginning; the last, p, is the seventh from the end; while the middle letter of the three, D, is in the
middle of the ivhole Psalm! — (Ed.)
“a,” may be thus expanded— (Ed.) :
a c|d | 1. “ Fret not.” (mnn i«)
I e[ 2. “ For.” (*2)
F | 3 —5- Trust, delight, commit.
F | 6, 7-. Trust, rest, wait.
CI d | -7, 8. “ Fret not.” (“innn
e( 9, 10. “For.” (*2)
“ b,” may be thus expanded :
b g | 12. Designs,
h j 13. Defeat.
g | 14. Designs (sword and bow).
h | 15. Defeat (sword and bow).


|)salm xxxviii.
A Psalm of David, to bring to remembrance. 1
A | i 0 Lord, rebuke me not in thy wrath : neither chasten me in thy hot displeasure.
B a 2 For thine arrows stick fast in me, and thy hand presseth me sore.
3 There is no soundness in my flesh because of thine anger; neither is there
any rest in my bones because of my sin. 4 For mine iniquities are gone
over mine head: as an heavy burden they are too heavy for me. 5 My
wounds stink and are corrupt because of my foolishness. 6 lam troubled;
lam bowed down greatly; Igo mourning all the day long. 7 For my loins
are filled with a loathsome disease : and there is no soundness in my flesh.
8 lam feeble and sore broken: I have roared by reason of the disquietness
of my heart. 9 Lord, all my desire is before thee; and my groaning is not
hid from thee. 10 My heart panteth, my strength faileth me: as for the
light of mine eyes, it also is gone from me.
b 11 My lovers and my friends stand aloof from my sore ; and my kinsmen
stand afar off. 12 They also that seek after my life lay snares for me:
and they that seek my hurt speak mischievous things, and imagine
deceits all the day long. 13 But I, as a deaf man, heard not; and I was
as a dumb man that openeth not his mouth. 14 Thus I was as a man
that heareth not, and in whose mouth are no reproofs. 15 For in thee,
0 Lord, do I hope: thou wilt hear, 0 Lord my God. 16 For I said,
Hear me, lest otherwise they should rejoice over me : when my foot slippeth,
they magnify themselves against me.
B a 17 For lam ready to halt, and my sorrow is continually before me. 18 For
I will declare mine iniquity; I will be sorry for my sin,
b 19 But mine enemies are lively, and they are strong: and they that hate
me wrongfully are multiplied. 20 They also that render evil for good are
mine adversaries ; because I follow the thing that good is.
A 2i Forsake me not, 0 Lord : 0 my God, be not far from me. 22 Make haste to
help me, 0 Lord my salvation.

C a 7 All that hate me whisper together against me: against me do they devise
my hurt.
h 8 An evil disease, say they , cleaveth fast unto him: and now that he
lieth he shall rise up no more.
c 9 Yea, mine own familiar friend, in whom 1 trusted, which did eat of
my bread, hath lifted up his heel against me.

In the MS. the Skeleton and Text did not agree, so we have carried out a pencilled note which
said “ alter.” Note that B and B set forth God’s operations on behalf of His people and Zion;
while I) and E set forth His operations in the world at large. Hence Psalm xlvii. answers to
1) and E, and Psalm xlviii. answers to B and B.

Lote. We have slightly developed the Skeleton arrangement as indicated by the author in
pencilled marks. In a and b note the alternation of “God” and “King.” Note also the double
parallels in B and B, teaching us that the people will be subdued (B) when the princes are gathered
together (B) ; and that His “ inheritance ” (B) is “ the people of the God of Abraham (B).” —(Ed.)

To the chief Musician, A Psalm for the sons of Korah.
II 1 Hear this, all ye people ; give ear, all ye inhabitants of the world : 2 Both
I low and high, rich and poor, together.
THEMA II 3My mouth shall speak of wisdom ; and the meditation of my heart shall he
of understanding. 4 I will incline mine ear to a parable : I will open my
dark saying upon the harp.
A a j 5 Wherefore should I fear in the days of evil,
| ivhen the iniquity of my heels shall compass me about ?
b 6 They that trust in their wealth, and boast themselves in the multitude of their riches ;
7 None of them can by any means redeem his brother, nor give to God a ransom for him :
8 (For the redemption of their soul is precious, and it cea-seth for ever :)
9 That he should still live for ever, and not see corruption.
c 10 For he seeth that wise men die,
likewise the fool and the brutish person perish,
and and 1 leave their wealth to others.
11 Their inward thought is, that their houses shall continue for ever,
and their dwelling places to all generations ;
they call their lands after their own names.
B | 12 Nevertheless man being in honour abideth not: he is like the beasts that perish.
Ad I 13 This their way is their folly :
I yet their posterity approve their sayings. Selah.
c 14 Like sheep they are laid in the grave ;
death shall feed on them ;
and the upright shall have dominion over them in the morning;
and their beauty shall consume in the grave from their dwelling.
h 15 But God will redeem my soul from the power of the grave :
| for he shall receive me. Selah.
a 16 Be not thou afraid when one is made rich, when the glory of his house is increased ;
17 For when he dieth he shall carry nothing away: his glory shall not descend after him.
18 Though while he lived he blessed his soul; and men will praise thee, when thou doest
well to thyself.
19 He shall go to the generation of his fathers; they shall never see light.
B | 20 Man that is in honour, and understandeth not, is like the beasts that perish.

1 They leave. Note that the couplets and quatrains in A and A are alternate in their
order, while the couplet in the one member is answered by the quatrain in the other member.— (Ed.)
The Thema, or prelude, consists of two successions, of a direct quatrain, followed by an introverted
one; anticipating the form of the Psalm itself. — (Ed.)

ssalm lyiii.
To the chief Musician, Al-taschith, Michtam of David.
A iDo ye indeed speak righteousness, 0 congregation? do ye judge uprightly, oye
sons of men? 2 Yea, in heart ye work wickedness; ye weigh the violence of
your hands in the earth. 3 The wicked are estranged from the womb : they go
astray as soon as they he horn, speaking lies. 4 Their poison is like the poison of
a serpent: they are like the deaf adder that stoppeth her ear; 5 Which will not
hearken to the voice of charmers, charming never so wisely. 6 Break their
teeth, 0 God, in their mouth: break out the great teeth of the young lions, O
Lord. 7 Let them melt away as waters which run continually : when he hendeth
his how to shoot his arrows, let them be as cut in pieces. BAs a snail which melteth,
let every one of them pass away : like the untimely birth of a woman, that they may
not see the sun. 9 Before your pots can feel the thorns, he shall take them away
as with a whirlwind, both living, and in his wrath.
810 The righteous shall rejoice when he seeth the vengeance :he shall wash his
feet in the blood of the wicked.
B 1 r So that a man shall say, Yerily there is a reward for the righteous :
A | verily he is a God that judgeth in the earth.

wdth their mouth, but they curse inwardly. Selah.

increase, set not your heart upon them.
C 11 God hath spoken once; twice have I heard this ; that power belongeth unto

To the chief Musician, A Psalm or Song of David.
Y I Let God arise, let his enemies be scattered; let them also that hate him flee
before him. 2 As smoke is driven away, so drive them away: as wax melteth
before the fire, so let the wicked perish at the presence of God.
Z 3 But let the righteous be glad; let them rejoice before God: yea, let them
exceedingly rejoice.
A I 4 Sing unto God, sing praises to his name : extol him that rideth upon the heavens by his name
1 JAH, and rejoice before him.
B aj 5 A father of the fatherless, and a judge of the widows, is God in his holy habitation.
| 6 God setteth the solitary in families ; he bringeth out those which are bound with chains:
b | but the rebellious dwell in a dry land.
c 7 0 God, when thou wentest forth before thy people, when thou didst march through
the wilderness; Selah : 8 The earth shook, the heavens also dropped at the presence
of God ; even Sinai itself was moved at the presence of God, the God of Israel. 9 Thou,
O God, didst send a plentiful rain, whereby thou didst confirm thine inheritance, when
it was weary. 10 Thy congregation hath dwelt therein: thou, 0 God, hast prepared
of thy goodness for the poor,
and 11 The Lord gave the word; great was the company of those that published if.
12 Kings of armies did flee apace : and she that tarried at home divided the spoil.
13 Though ye have lien among the pots, 1 yet shall ye be as the wings of a dove
covered with silver, and her feathers with yellow gold. 14 When the Almighty 2
scattered kings in it, it was white as snow in Salmon.

A Psalm of Asaph.
A. | i Truly God is good to Israel, even to such as are of a clean heart.
B( 2 But as for me, my feet were almost gone; my steps had well nigh slipped.
C | 3 For I was envious at the foolish, when I saw the prosperity of the wicked.
D 4 For there are no bands in their death; but their strength is firm. 5 They are not
in trouble as other men ; neither are they plagued like other men. 6 Therefore pride
compasseth them about as a chain 1 ; violence eovereth them as a garment. 7 Their
eyes stand out with fatness: they have more than heart could wish. 8 They are
corrupt, and speak wickedly concerning oppression: they speak loftily. 9 They set
their mouth against the heavens, and their tongue walketh through the earth.
10 Therefore his people return hither 2 : and waters of a full cup are wrung out to them.
11 And they say, How doth God know ? and is there knowledge in the Most High '<
12 Behold, these are the ungodly, who prosper in the world ; they increase in riches.
E 13 Yerily I have cleansed my heart in vain, and washed my hands in innocencv.
14 For all the day long have I been plagued, and chastened every morning. 15 If
I say, I will speak thus ; behold, 1 should offend against the generation ot thy
children. 16 When I thought to know this, it teas too painful for me; 17 Until I
went into the sanctuary of God ; then understood I their end.
D 18 Surely thou didst set them in slippery places: thou castedst them down into
destruction. 19 How are they brought into desolation, as in a moment ! they are
utterly consumed with terrors. 20 Asa dream when one awaketh; so, 0 Lord, when
thou awakest, thou shalt despise their image.
C | 21 Thus 3 my heart was grieved, and I was pricked in my reins.
B | 22 So foolish was I, and ignorant: I was as a beast before thee.
A 23 Nevertheless lam continually with thee: thou hast holden me by my right hand. 24 Thou
shalt guide me with thy counsel, and afterward receive me to glory. 25 Whom have I in
heaven but thee f and there is none upon earth that I desire beside thee. 26 My flesh and my
heart fuileth: but God is the strength of my heart, and my portion for ever. 27 For, 10, they
that are far from thee shall perish : thou hast destroyed all them that go a whoring from thee.
28 But it is good for me to draw near to God: I have put my trust in the Lord God, 1 that I may
declare all thy works.

ssalm lxxiv.
Maschil of Asaph.
A i 0 God, why hast thou cast us off for ever? why doth thine anger smoke against
the sheep of thy pasture? 2 Remember thy congregation, which thou hast pur-
chased of old; the rod of thine inheritance, which thou hast redeemed; this mount
Zion, wherein thou hast dwelt. 3 Lift up thy feet unto the perpetual desolations;
even all that the enemy hath done wickedly in the sanctuary. 4 Thine enemies
roar in the midst of thy congregations; they set up their ensigns for signs. 5 A
man was famous according as he had lifted up axes upon the thick trees. 6 But
now they break down the carved work thereof at once with axes and hammers.
7 They have cast fire into thy sanctuary, they have defiled by casting down the
dwelling place of thy name to the ground. 8 They said in their hearts, Let us
destroy them together: they have burned up all the synagogues of God in the
land. 9We see not our signs: there is no more any prophet; neither is there
among us any that knoweth how long. 10 0 God, how long shall the adversary
reproach? shall the enemy blaspheme thy name for ever? 11 Why withdrawest
thou thy hand, even thy right hand? pluck it out of thy bosom.
B 12 Bor God is my King of old, working salvation in the midst of the earth.
813 Thou didst divide the sea by thy strength: thou brakest the heads of the
dragons in the waters. 14 Thou brakest the heads of leviathan in pieces, and
gavest him to he meat to the people inhabiting the wilderness. Thou didst
cleave the fountain and the flood; thou driedst up mighty rivers. 16 The day
is thine, the night also is thine: thou hast prepared the light and the sun.
17 Thou hast set all the borders of the earth: thou hast made summer and
winter.
A 1 18 Remember this, that the enemy hath reproached, 0 Loud, and that the foolish
1 people have blasphemed thy name. 19 0 deliver not the soul of thy turtledove
i unto the multitude of the wicked: forget not the congregation of thy poor for ever.
20 Have respect unto the covenant: for the dark places of the earth are full of
the habitations of cruelty. 21 O let not the oppressed return ashamed: let the
poor and needy praise thy name. 22 Arise, O God, plead thine own cause;
remember how the foolish man reproacheth thee daily. 23 Forget not the voice
of thine enemies: the tumult of those that rise up against thee increaseth con-
tinually.

The Editor suggests the following supplementary description of the same structure: —

A | 10—12. Occupation with God.
B | 13 -20. Its result —happiness. (See Psalm Ixxiii. for a similar cause and effect.)

Itealm lxxix.
A Psalm of Asaph.
A i 0 God, the heathen are come into thine inheritance; thy holy temple have
they defiled; they have laid Jerusalem on heaps. 2 The dead bodies of thy
servants have they given to he meat unto the fowls of the heaven, the flesh of thy
saints unto the bea-Js of the earth. 3 Their blood have they shed like water
round about Jerusalem; and there was none to bury them.
B 4 We are become a reproach to our neighbours, a scorn and derision to them
that are round about us.
A 5 How long, Lord? wilt thou be angry for ever? shall thy jealousy burn like
fire ? 6 Pour out thy wrath upon the heathen that have not known thee, and
upon the kingdoms that have not called upon thy name. 7 For they have
devoured Jacob, and laid waste his dwelling place. 8 0 remember not against us
former iniquities : let thy tender mercies speedily prevent us : for we are brought
very low. 9 Help us, O God of our salvation, for the glory of thy name: and
deliver us, and purge away our sins, for thy name’s sake. 10 Wherefore should
the heathen say, Where is their God ? let him be known among the heathen in our
sight by the revenging of the blood of thy servants which is shed. 11 Let the
sighing of the prisoner come before thee; according to the greatness of thy power
preserve thou those that are appointed to die;
B i 2 And render unto our neighbours sevenfold into their bosom their reproach,
wherewith they have reproached thee, 0 Lord. 13 So we thy people and sheep
of thy pasture will give thee thanks for ever: we will shew forth thy praise to
all generations.

root, and it filled the land. 10 The hills were covered with the shadow of it,

cause thy face to shine; and we shall be saved.

ssalm lxxxiv.
To the chief Musician upon Gittifch, A Psalm for the sons of Korah.
A a j How amiable are thy tabernacles, 0 Lord of hosts ! 2My soul longeth, rea
even fainteth for the courts of the Lord : my heart and my flesh crieth out for
the living God. 3 Yea, the sparrow hath found an house, and the swallow a
nest for herself, where she may lay her young, even thine altars, O Lord of hosts,
my King, and my God. 4 Blessed are they that dwell in thy house : they will
be still praising thee. Selah.
b 3 Blessed is the man whose strength is in thee; in whose heart are the ways
of them. 6 Who passing through the valley of Baca make it a well; the
rain also filleth the pools. 7 They go from strength to strength, every one of
them in Zion appeareth before God.
B | 8 0 Lord God of hosts, hear my prayer: give ear, 0 God of Jacob. Selah.
B | 9 Behold, 0 God our shield, and look upon the face of thine Anointed.
A a 10 For a day in thy courts is better than a thousand. I had rather be a door-
keeper in the house of my God, than to dwell in the tents of wickedness.
b 11 For the Lord God is a sun and shield: the Lord will give grace and
glory: no good thing will he withhold from them that walk uprightly.
12 O Lord of hosts, blessed is the man that trusteth in thee.
Psalm LXXXIY. — The Skeleton.
A j a | I—4.1 —4. Blessedness of dwellers.
b | 5 —7. Blessedness of approaehers.

B | 9. Prayer.
A [a | 10. Blessedness of dwellers (a). [*d “for.”]
h | 11, 12. Blessedness of approaehers (b). [>3 “for.”]
The Editor offers the following arrangement of “ a” as an illustration of the way in
which the sense of a passage is made clear by observing its structure. Here,
in “ and,” we observe that the “ altars ” are connected with the Psalmist’s desire , as
in“ and,” and not with the swallow’s nest. Let “and ” and “and” be read connectedly ;
“ e ” and “ e ” being thus practically in a parenthesis.
Note also that in “A” we have the grounds of the blessedness mentioned in A :
“a” answering to “ a,” and “ b ” answering to “ b.”—(Ed.)
a c | 1 How amiable are thy tabernacles, 0 Lord of hosts!
and 2 My soul longeth, yea, even fainteth for the courts of the Lord : my heart
and my flesh crieth out for the living God.
e | 3 Yea, the sparrow hath found an house,
e | and the swallow a nest for herself, where she may lay her young,
and ( even thine altars, O Lord of hosts, my King, and my God.
c I 4 Blessed are they that dwell in thy house: they will be still praising thee.
I Selah.

observing the structure, in which singular corresponds with singular , and plural with
plural :■ —

ssalm lxxxv.
To the chief Musician, A Psalm for the sons of Korah.
A I Lord, thou hast been favourable unto thy land : thou hast brought back the
captivity of Jacob. 2 Thou hast forgiven the iniquity of thy people, thou hast
covered all their sin. Selah. 3 Thou hast taken away all thy wrath: thou hast
turned thyself from the fierceness of thine anger.
Ba 1 4 Turn us, 0 God of our salvation, and cause thine anger toward us to cease,
b 3 Wilt thou be angry with us for ever ? wilt thou draw out thine anger
to all generations ? 6 Wilt thou not revive us again: that thy people
may rejoice in thee?
B a | 7 Shew us thy mercy, 0 Lord, and grant us thy salvation.
h 8 1 will hear what God the Lord will speak; for he will speak peace
unto his people, and to his saints: but let them not turn 1 again to folly.
A 9 Surely his salvation is nigh them that fear him; that glory may dwell in our
land. 10 Mercy and truth are met together; righteousness and peace have kissed
each other. 11 Truth shall spring out of the earth; and righteousness shall look
down from heaven. 12 Yea, the Lord shall give that which is good ; and our land
shall yield her increase, t 3 Righteousness shall go before him; and shall set us
in the way of his steps.

ssalm lxxxvi.
A Prayer of David.
A i Bow down thine ear, 0 Lord, hear me: for lam poor and needy. 2 Preserve
my soul; for lam holy; O thou my God, save thy servant that trusteth in thee.
3 Be merciful unto me, 0 Lord: for I cry unto thee daily. 4 Rejoice the soul of
thy servant: for unto thee, O Lord, do I lift up my soul. 5 For thou, Lord, art
good, and ready to forgive; and plenteous in mercy unto all them that call upon
thee. 6 Give ear, 0 Lord, unto my prayer; and attend to the voice of my
supplications.
B a | 7 In the day of my trouble I will call upon thee :
h | for thou wilt answer me.
C | 8 Among the gods there is none like unto thee, 0 Lord;
C | neither are there any works like unto thy works.
Bag All nations whom thou hast made shall come and worship before thee,
O Lord; and shall glorify thy name.
h | 1 o For thou art great, and doest wondrous things : thou art God alone.
A 11 Teach me thy way, O Lord ; I will walk in thy truth : unite my heart to fear
thy name. 12 I will praise thee, O Lord my God, with all my heart: and I will
glorify thy name for evermore. 13 For great is thy mercy toward me : and thou
hast delivered my soul from the lowest hell. 14 O God, the proud are risen
against me, and the assemblies of violent men have sought after my soul; and
have not set thee before them. 15 But thou, 0 Lord, art a God full of compassion,
and gracious, longsuffering, and plenteous in mercy and truth. 16 0 turn unto
me, and have mercy upon me ; give thy strength unto thy servant, and save the son
lof thine handmaid. 17 Shew me a token for good; that they which hate me may
I see it , and be ashamed: because thou, Lord, hast holpen me, and comforted me.

A Song or Psalm for the sons of Korah, to the chief Musician upon Mahalath Leannoth, Maschil of

A i O Lord God of my salvation, I have cried day and night before thee: 2 Let
my prayer come before thee: incline thine ear unto my cry;
B 3 For my soul is full of troubles: and my life draweth nigh unto the grave.
4 I am counted with them that go down into the pit: I am as a man that hath
no strength: 5 Free among the dead, like the slain that lie in the grave,
whom thou rememberest no more: and they are cut off from thy hand. 6 Thou
hast laid me in the lowest pit, in darkness, in the deeps.
C 7 Thy wrath lieth hard upon me, 1 and thou hast afflicted me with all thy
waves. Selah.
D 8 Thou hast put away mine acquaintance far from me; thou hast made
me an abomination unto them; lam shut up, and I cannot come forth.
9 Mine eye mourneth by reason of affliction:
A Lord, I have called daily upon thee, I have stretched out my hands unto thee.
10 Wilt thou shew wonders to the dead? shall Ihe dead arise and praise thee?
Selah. 11 Shall thy lovingkindness be declared in the grave ?or thy faithful-
ness in destruction? 12 Shall thy wonders be known in the dark? and thy
righteousness in the land of forgetfulness? J 3 But unto thee have I cried, O
Lord; and in the morning shall my prayer prevent thee. 14 Lord, why castest
thou off my soul ? why hidest thou thy face from me ?
B 15 lam afflicted and ready to die from my youth up : while I suffer thy terrors
1 am distracted.
G 16 Thy fierce wrath goeth over me 1 ; thy terrors have cut me off. 17 They
came round about me daily like water; they compassed me about together.
D 18 Lover and friend hast thou put far from me, and mine acquaintance
. into darkness.

ssalm lxxxix
Maschil of Ethan the Ezrahite.
A 1 1 I will sing of the mercies of the Lord for ever : with my mouth will I make known thy faithful-
Iness 1 to all generations. . ,
B a 2 For I have said, 2 Mercy shall be built up for ever: thy faithfulness shplt thou establish in
the very heavens. 3 I have made a covenant with my chosen, I have sworn unto David my
servant, 4 Thy seed will I establish for ever, and build up thy throne to all generations.
b 5 And the heavens shall praise thy wonders, O Lord : thy faithfulness also in the
congregation of the saints. 6 For who in the heaven can be compared unto the Lord ? who
among the sons of the mighty* can be likened unto the Lord ? 7 God is greatly to be
feared in the assembly of the saints, and to be had in reverence of all them that are
about him. 8 0 Lord God of hosts, who is a strong LORD like unto thee ? or to thy
faithfulness round about thee ? 9 Thou rulest the raging of the sea : when the waves
thereof arise, thou stillest them. 10 Thou hast broken Bahab in pieces, as one that is
slain ; thou hast scattered thine enemies with thy strong arm. 11 The heavens are thine,
the earth also is thine: as for the world and the fulness thereof, thou hast founded them.
12 The north and the south thou hast created them : Tabor and Hermon shall rejoice in
thy name. 13 Thou hast a mighty arm : strong is thy hand, and high is thy right hand.
14 Justice and judgment are the habitation of thy throne : mercy and truth shall go before
thy face. 15 Blessed is the people that know the joyful sound: they shall walk, O Lord,
in the light of thy countenance. 16 In thy name shall they rejoice all the day : and in
thy righteousness shall they be exalted. 17 For thou art the glory of their strength :^ TIC
in thy favour our horn shall be exalted. 18 For the Lord is our defence ; and the Holy
One of Israel is our king.
Bn 19 Then thou spakest in vision to thy holy one, and saidst, I have Laid help upon one that is
mighty; I have exalted one chosen out of the people. 20 I have found David my servant; with
my holy oil have I anointed him: 21 With whom my hand shall be established: mine arm
also shall strengthen him. 22 The enemy shall not exact upon him ; nor the son of wickedness
afflict him. 23 And I will beat down his foes before his face, and plague them that hate him.
24 But my faithfulness and my mercy shall he with him : and in my name shall his horn be
exalted. 25 I will set his hand also in the sea, and his right hand in the rivers. 26 He shall
cry unto me, Thou art my father, my God, and the rock of my salvation. 27 Also I will make
him my firstborn, higher 4 than 5 the kings of the earth. 28 My mercy will I keep for
I him for evermore, and my covenant shall stand, fast with him. 29 His seed also wil
I make to endicre for ever, and his throne as the days of heaven. 30 If his children
forsake my law, and walk not in my judgments; 31 If they break my statutes, and keep not
my commandments ; 32 Then will I visit their transgression with the rod, and their iniquity
with stripes. 33 Nevertheless my lovingkindness will I not utterly take from him, nor saner
my faithfulness to fail. 34 My covenant will I not break, nor alter the thing that is gone out
I of my lips. 35 Once have I sworn by my holiness that 1 will not lie unto David. 36 His seed
shall endure for ever, and his throne as the sun before me. 37 P shall be established for ever
as the moon, and as a faithful witness in heaven. Selah.
b 38 But thou hast cast off and abhorred, thou hast been wroth with thine Anointed.
39 Thou hast made void the covenant of thy servant: thou hast profaned his crown by
casting it to the ground. 40 Thou hast broken down all his hedges ; thou hast brought
his strong holds to ruin. 41 All that pass by the way spoil him : he is a reproach to his
neighbours. 42 Thou hast set up the right hand of his adversaries; thou hast made all
his enemies to rejoice. 43 Thou hast also turned the edge of his sword, and hast not
made him to stand in the battle. 44 Thou hast made his glory to cease, and cast his
throne down to the ground. 45 The days of his youth hast thou shortened: thou hast
covered him with shame. Selah. 46 How long, Lord ? wilt thou hide thyself for ever i
shall thy wrath burn like fire ? 47 Remember how short my time is ; wherefore hast
thou made all men in vain ?48 What man is he that liveth, and shall not see death.
shall he deliver his soul from the hand of the grave? Selah. 49 Lord, where are thy
former lovingkindnesses, which thou swarest unto David in thy truth ? 5° Remembei,
Lord, the reproach of thy servants; how Ido bear in my bosom the reproach of all the
mighty people ; 51 Wherewith thine enemies have reproached, 0 Lord ; wherewith they
have reproached the footsteps of thine Anointed.
A| 52 Blessed he the Lord for evermore. Amen, and Amen.

s)salm xc.
A Prayer of Moses the man of God.
A i Lord, thou hast been our dwelling place in all generations. 2 Before the
mountains were brought forth, or ever thou hadst formed the earth and the world
even from everlasting to everlasting, thou art God. *
B 3 Thou turnest man to destruction; and sayest, Return, ye children of men.
4 lor a thousand years in thy sight are hut as yesterday when it is past, and as a
watch in the night, 5 Thou carriest them away as with a flood; they are as a
sleep : in the morning they are like grass which groweth up. 6ln the morning it
nourisheth and groweth up; in the evening it is cut down, and withereth. 7 For
we are consumed by thine anger, and by thy wrath are we troubled 8 Thou
hast set our iniquities before thee, our secret sins in the light of thy countenance,
y oi all our days are passed away in thy wrath; we spend our years as a tale
that is told. 10 The days of our years are threescore years and ten; and if by
reason of strength they he fourscore years, yet is their strength labour and sorrow;
for it is soon cut off, and we fly away. 11 Who knoweth the power of thine anger ?
even according to thy fear, so is thy wrath.
C 12 S° teach us to number our days, that we may apply our hearts unto wisdom.
13 Return, O Lord, how long? and let it repent thee concerning thy servants.
14 O satisfy us early with thy mercy; that we may rejoice and be glad all our
dajs. 13 Make us glad according to the days wherein thou hast afflicted us, an I
the years wherein we have seen evil. 16 Let thy work appear unto thy servants,
and thy glory unto their children. 17 And let the beauty of the Lord our God
be upon us: and establish thou the work of our hands upon us; yea, the work of
our hands establish thou it.

A 1 Lord, thou hast been our dwelling place in all generations. 2 Before the
mountains were brought forth, or ever thou hadst formed the earth and the world,
even from everlasting to everlasting,"thou art God.
B | 3 Thou turnest man to destruction;

A 4 For a thousand years in thy sight are hut as yesterday when it is past, and as
a watch in the night.
B 3 Thou carriest them away as with a flood; they are as a sleep: in the moxming
they are like grass which groweth up. 6ln the morning it flourisheth, and
groweth up; in the evening it is cut down, and withereth. 7 For we are
consumed by thine anger, and by thy wrath are we troubled. 8 Thou hast set
our iniquities before thee, our secret sins in the light of thy countenance. 9 For
all our days are passed away in thy wrath: we spend our years as a tale that
is told. 10 The days of our years are threescore years and ten; and if by reason
of strength they he fourscore years, yet is their strength labour and sorrow; for
it is soon cut off, and we fly away. 1 r Who knoweth the power of thine anger ?
even according to thy fear, so is thy wrath.
C 12 So teach us to number our days, that we may apply our hearts unto
wisdom. 13 Return, 0 Lord, how long? and let it repent thee concerning
thy servants. 14 0 satisfy us early with thy mercy; that we may rejoice and
be glad all our days. 15 Make us glad according to the days wherein thou
hast afflicted us, and the years wherein we have seen evil. t 6 Let thy work
appear unto thy servants, and thy glory unto their children. 17 And let the
beauty of the Lord our God be upon us: and establish thou the work of our

ipsalm xciii.
A The Lord reigneth, 1 he is clothed with majesty; the Lord is clothed with
strength, wherewith he hath girded himself; the world also is stablished, that it
cannot be moved. 2 Thy throne is established of old ; thou art from everlasting.

Psalm XCIII. —The Skeleton.
A 1 1,2. The Lord. Eternity.
B| 3. The floods’ voices. The floods’ waves.
B| 4. The waters’ noise. The waves’ might.
A\ 5. The Lord. Eternity.
1 There are three Psalms that commence with the words “The Lord Reigneth,'’ viz., xciii.,
xcvii., and xcix. They each end with a reference to holiness. Ps. xciii., “Holiness becometh
Thine house, 0 Lord, for ever.” Ps. xcvii., “ Give thanks at the remembrance of His holiness;”
and the third Psalm (xcix.) has it three times: “It is holy” (f. 3), “He is holy” ( v . 5), “The
Lord our God is holy ” (v, 9).
This fact seems to say to us that when the Lord reigns all will be holy; that when His
kingdom comes, His name will he hallowed on earth as it is in heaven. “In that day there shall
be upon the hells (or bridles) of the horses, HOLINESS UNTO THE LORD ; and the pots in the
Lord’s house shall be like the howls before the altar. Yea, every pot in Jerusalem and in Judah
shall be holiness unto the Lord of hosts” (Zech. xiv. 20, 21-). “Her merchandise and her hire
shall be holiness to the Lord” (Is. xxiii. 18).
Is this why the four living creatures who call for the judgments which will issue in the Lord’s
reign do so with the threefold cry of these three Psalms, “ Holy, holy, holy”? (Rev. iv. 8). — (Ed.)

A a i Hear my prayer, O Lord, and let my cry come unto thee. 2 Hide not thy
face from me in the day when I am in trouble; incline thine ear unto me: in
the day when I call answer me speedily.
h 3 For my days are consumed like smoke, and my hones are burned as an
hearth. 4 My heart is smitten, and withered like grass ; so that I forget to
eat my bread. 5 By reason of the voice of my groaning my bones cleave to
my skin. 6I am like a pelican of the wilderness : lam like an owl of the
desert. 7 I watch, and am as a sparrow alone upon the house top. 8 Mine
enemies reproach me all the day; and they that are mad against me are
sworn against me. 9 For I have eaten ashes like bread, and mingled my
drink with weeping, 10 Because of thine indignation and thy wrath: for
thou hast lifted me up, and cast me down. 11 My days are like a shadow
that declineth ; and I am withered like grass.
B 1 2 But thou, 0 Lord, shalt endure for ever ; and thy remembrance unto
all generations.
C r 3 Thou shalt arise, and have mercy upon Zion : for the time to favour
her, yea, the set time, is come. 14 For thy servants take pleasure in
her stones, and favour the dust thereof. 15 So the heathen shall fear
the name of the Lord, and all the kings of the earth thy glory.
16 When the Lord shall build up Zion, he shall appear in his glory.
1 7 He will regard the prayer of the destitute, and not despise their
prayer. 18 This shall be written for the generation to come : and the
people which shall be created shall praise THE LORD. 19 For he
hath looked down from the height of his sanctuary ; from heaven did

ssalm cm.
A Psalm of David.
A i Bless the Lord, 0 my soul: and all that is within me, bless his holy name.
2 Bless the Lord, omy soul, and forget not all his benefits; 3 Who forgiveth
all thine iniquities; who healeth all thy diseases; 4 Who redeemeth thy life
from destruction; who crowneth thee with lovingkindness and tender mercies;
5 Who satisfieth thy mouth with good things; so that thy youth is renewed like
the eagle’s.
B 6 The Lord executeth righteousness and judgment for all that are oppressed.
7 lie made known his ways unto Moses, his acts unto the children of Israel.
C | 8 The Lord is merciful and gracious, slow to anger, and plenteous in mercy.
D | 9 He will not always chide: neither will he keep his anger for ever.
E 10 He hath not dealt with us after our sins ; nor rewarded us according
to our iniquities.
F 1 r For as the heaven is high above the earth, so great is his mercy
toward them that fear him. 12 As far as the east is from the west, so
far hath he removed our transgressions from us. 13 Like as a father
pitieth his children, so the Lord pitieth them that fear him.
D 14 For he knoweth our frame ; he remembereth that we are dust, 13 As
for man, his days are as grass: as a flower of the field, so he flourisheth.
16 For the wind passeth over it, and it is gone; and the place thereof
shall know it no more.
C 17 But the mercy of the Lord is Horn everlasting to everlasting upon them
that fear him, and his righteousness unto children’s children; 18 To such
as keep his covenant, and to those that remember his commandments to do
them.
B 19 The Lord hath prepared his throne in the heavens; and his kingdom ruleth
over all.
A 20 Bless the Lord, ye his angels, that excel in strength, that do his command-
ments, hearkening unto the voice of his word. 21 Bless ye the Lord, all ye his
hosts ;ye ministers of his, that do his pleasure. 22 Bless the Lord, all his works
in all places of his dominion: bless the Lord, 0 ray soul.

ssalm civ.
A 1 Bless the Lord, 0 my soul. .
B 0 Lord my God, thou art very great; thou art clothed with honour and majesty.
2 Who coverest thyself with light as with a garment; who stretchest out the
heavens like a curtain :
B 3 Who layeth the beams of his chambers in the waters: who maketh the
clouds his chariot: who walketh upon the wings of the wind: 4 Who
maketh his angels spirits; his ministers a flaming fire: 3 Who laid the
foundations of the earth, that it should not be removed for ever.
C 6 Thou coveredst it with the deep as with a garment: the waters stood above
the mountains. 7 At thy rebuke they fled; at the voice of thy thunder they
hasted away. 8 They go up by the mountains; they go down by the valleys
unto the place which thou hast founded for them. 9 Thou hast set a bound
that they may not pass over; that they turn not again to cover the earth.
C 10 He sendeth the springs into the valleys, which run among the hills.
11 They give drink to every beast of the field: the wild asses quench theii
thirst, 12 By them shall the fowls of the heaven have their habitation, which
sing among the branches. 13 He watereth the hills from his chambers :
D 1 the earth is satisfied with the fruit of thy works.
I) 14 He causeth the grass to grow for the cattle, and herb for the service ot
man: that he may bring forth food out of the earth; 15 And wine that
maketh glad the heart of man, and oil to make his face to shine, and bread
which strengthened man’s heart. 16 The trees of the Lord are full of sap;
the cedars of Lebanon, which he hath planted; 17 W r here the birds make
their nests: as for the stork, the fir trees are her house. 18 The high hills
are a refuge for the wild goats; and the rocks for the conies. 19 He
appointed the moon for seasons: the sun knoweth his going down.
E 20 Thou makest darkness, and it is night: wherein all the beasts of the forest
do creep forth. . r
E 21 The young lions roar after their prey, and seek their meat from Hod.
22 The sun ariseth, they gather themselves together, and lay them down in
their dens. 23 Man goeth forth unto his work and to his labour until the
evening. _
F 24 0 Lord, how manifold are thy works ! in wisdom hast thou made them all:
the earth is full of thy riches. 25 So is this great and wide sea, wherein
are things creeping innumerable, both small and great beasts. 26 There
go the ships; there is that leviathan, whom thou hast made to play therein.
27 These wait all upon thee; that thou mayest give them their meat in due
season. 28 That thou givest them they gather: thou openest thine hand, they
are filled with good. 29 Thou hidest thy face, they are troubled : thou takest
away their breath, they die, and return to their dust. 30 Thou sendest forth
thy spirit, they are created; and thou renewest the face of the earth.
F 3 1 The glory of the Lord shall endure for ever; the Lord shall rejoice in
his works. 32 He looketh on the earth, and it trembleth: he toucheth the
hills, and they smoke.
A 33 I will sing unto the Lord as long as I live: I will sing praise to my God while
I have my being. 34 My meditation of him shall be sweet; I will be glad in the
Lord. 35 Let the sinners be consumed out of the earth, and let the wicked be no
more. Bless thou the Lord, omy soul. Praise ye THE LORD 1 .

Note.— That A and A are hortatory, and in the second person plural. All the rest of the
Psalm is in the third person. In B and Bwe have God’s remembrance of His covenant; but
in B it is in promise (“I ivill give”), while in Bit is in performance {“and He gave”). C and
C consist of narrative: in Cwe have the history of the patriarchs (as recorded in Genesis), and
in C'the corresponding history of the nation (as recorded in Exodus). — (Ed.)
The two members, B and B, may be thus arranged:— (Ed.)
B e | B—lo.8 —10. The Covenant remembered,
f 1 11. The land given,
g | 12. The People described.
B e | 42, 43. The Covenant remembered.
f | 44. The land inherited.
g | 45-. The People described.
The two members, “ d ” and “ d,” may also be further arranged : — (Ed.)
d h | 17. The sending of the deliverer,
i | 18, 19. His trial by the word,
k 1 20 —22. The deliverance.
d h | 26. The sending of the deliverers.
1 I 27 —36. Egypt’s trial by the word {v. 27, margin,
1 “ Heb. words of his signs ”).
k | 27 —41. The deliverance.

are at their wit’s end. 28 Then they cry unto the Lord in their trouble, and he
bringeth them out of their distresses. 29 He maketh the storm a calm, so that the

bringeth them unto their desired haven.
and 31 Oh that men would praise the Lord for his goodness, and/or his wonderful works

ssalm cix.
To the chief Musician, A Psalm of David.
A i Hold not thy peace, 0 God of my praise ; 2 For the mouth of the wicked and the mouth of
the deceitful are opened against me : they have spoken against me with a lying tongue. 3 They
compassed me about also with words of hatred ; and fought against me without a cause.
4 For my love they are ray adversaries: but I give myself unto prayer. 5 And they have
rewarded me evil for good, and hatred for my love.
B 6 Set thou a wicked man over him: and let Satan stand at his right hand. 7 When he
shall be judged, let him be condemned : and let his prayer become sin. 8 Let his days be
few ; and let another take his office. 9 Let his children be fatherless, and his wife a widow.
10 Let his children be continually vagabonds, and beg : let them seek their bread also out of
their desolate places. 11 Let the extortioner catch all that he hath ; and let the strangers
spoil his labour. 12 Let there be none to extend mercy unto him: neither let there be
any to favour his fatherless children. 13 Let his posterity be cut off; and in the
generation following let their name be blotted out. 14 Let the iniquity of his fathers be
remembered with the Lord ; and let not the sin of his mother be blotted out. 15 Let them
be before the Lord continually, that he may cut off the memory of them from the earth.
16 Because that he remembered not to shew mercy, but persecuted the poor and needy man,
that he might even slay the broken in heart. 17 As he loved cursing, so let it come unto
him: as he delighted not in blessing, so let it be.far from him. 18 As he clothed himself
with cursing like as with his garment, so let it come into his bowels like water, and like oil
into his bones. 19 Let it be unto him as the garment which covereth him, and for a girdle
wherewith he is girded continually. 20 Let this he the reward of mine adversaries from the
Lord, and of them that speak evil against my soul.
A 21 But do thou for me, 0 God 1 the Lord, for thy name’s sake: because thy mercy is good,
deliver thou me. 22 For lam poor and needy, and my heart is wounded within me. 23 lam
gone like the shadow when it declineth; lam tossed up and down as the locust. 24 My knees
are weak through fasting ; and my flesh faileth of fatness. 25 I became also a reproach unto
j them : token they looked upon me they shaked their heads. 26 Hel p me, 0 Lord my God : 0 save
jme according to thy mercy ; 27 That they may know that this is thy hand ; that thou, Lord,
I hast done it. 28 Let them curse, but bless thou:
B when they arise, let them be ashamed; but let thy servant rejoice. 3 29 Let mine adversaries
be clothed 'with shame, and let them cover themselves with their own confusion, as with a
mantle. 30 I will greatly praise the Lord with my mouth ; yea, I will praise him among the
multitude. 31 For he shall stand at the right hand of the poor, to save him from those that
condemn his soul.

Notes on Psalm CXIX.
The Author has left nothing in manuscript concerning this Psalm, and it was originally
intended to print it as it stands in all our printed Bibles. But the Editor has been led to offer an
arrangement of his own, with the following notes upon the structure of this Psalm.
It is one of the so-called acrostic Psalms. It consists of 176 Massoretic verses, divided into
twenty-two groups. Each group thus consists of eight verses, and each of these eight verses begins
with the same letter. For example, the first eight verses each begin with Aleph, m (A), the second
eight verses each begin with Beth, a (B), and so on through the alphabet. As the Hebrew alpha-
bet consists of hventy-tivo letters, there is thus one letter for each group. It is next to impossible
to carry this out in another language, except by a very free translation, or at the expense of
accuracy. It may, however, be illustrated ; for it so happens that the ninth portion (verses 6$ —72),
in which each verse begins in Hebrew with Teth, id (T), also begins in the Authorised Version with
the letter Tin every verse but two, viz., 67 and 71. If we change the word “Before” (v. 67)
to Till, and the words “It is” (v. 71) to ’ Tin, then it will exactly represent the Hebrew
original:—
65. Thou hast dealt well with thy servant, 0 Lord,
according unto thy word.
66. Teach me good judgment and knowledge :
for I have believed thy commandments.


6-. Till I ivas afflicted I went astray: j kept % word ,
68. Thou art good, and doest good; ftjr
69. The proud have forged a lie against me: my „ hole heart ,
7 0. Their heart is as fat as grease; k fty Uw
7.. ’Tit good for me that I have been afflicted;; fty statutcs .
73. The law of thy mouth is better unto rf and silrer
Another peculiarity in the structure of Ps. cxix. is the recurrence of Ten to
the “Ten Words” of the Law given at Sinai). These have been so variously numbered and cited
hv expositors that we prefer to give them on the authority of the Massorah. , t tt +
7 The llubrick, on verse 122, is as follows Throughout the whole of the great alphabet
[i e the Alphabetic Psalm, cxix.] there is in every verse one of the following ten expressions.
L, ’ (Derech P Way), m» (Eduth, Testimony). D'nfß (Pikkudeem, npm (Mitzvah,
dlmandnLnts), (Imrah, Saying), noin (Torah. (Mishpat a oommant
It ¥ Ue„asness), pn (Chok. Statutes). (Davar, Word), which correspond to th Ten Command
ments: except one verse in which there is none of these, viz., verse 122. ( assora ,
Gm! The of the Psalm is based on these “Ten Words,” and yet there are no vain
repetitions. We give a brief definition of each. . ..
1. “ Wav,” Tpi (Derech), from to tread with the feet, means the act of treading or wa
in,j ; a going, wag, or journeying. It occurs thirteen times, viz., verses I, 3,5, 14.
3 ’ 3 2 3 _’ “ 7 Testimonies,” rin? (Edoth), occurs fourteen times (always in plural). It is from tv, to
turn back again, go over again, to say again and again, reiterate, hence to testify. tot 1 ereore
means that the Law is the Lord’s own testimony and witness concerning Himself and His attribu .
, « Precepts,” Q'7?e (Pikkudeem) (only found in the Psalms) occurs twenty-one times (aiwajs
plural). It is from igß, to strike or light upon any person or thing ; hence, to goto see, to visit,
to inspect, to superintend: then to give the oversight, enjoin. The pikkudeem are t e man ats or
things which God has charged His people with, and enjoined upon them, „
4. “ Commandments,” ntp (Mitzvah) occurs twenty-two times (all plural but one). Irom
nu? to setup, constitute, appoint, to command. Hence, Mitzvah means a
5. “Word,” Pro* (Imrah) occurs nineteen times, and is rendered “Word.’ {“Hoi s
only once, cf. Ps. xii. 6, the only other place in the Psalms where the plural is found). Hence we
must give the verses, in order to distinguish it from No. 10, w (Davar), viz., verses t i 38, 41,
50, 58,67, 76, 82, 103 {pi.), 116, 123, 133, 140, 148, 154, 158, 162, 170 and 172. ewo
expressions for the one translation thus occur forty-two times (6 * 7). Imrah, is from . T ,
to bring forth, bring to light, hence to say. Unlike ™it is followed by the words spoken. Hence,
Imrah means a saying, the word by which a revelation is imparted, while Davar (No. ioj
refers to the substance or the subject-matter of that revelation.
6. “Law,” rrjin (Torah) occurs twenty-five times (always singular). It is from to projec,
and hence, to point out, to show (Prov. vi. 13), then to instruct, teach. The Torah contains t e
Instructions of Jehovah to His people, pointing out to them His will. _ . „
7. “ Judgment,” ©Binn (Mishpat) occurs twenty-three times (always in plural except tour
times). It is from tDE®, to set upright, erect (Germ, richten), hence, to judge. Mishpat means
- judgment. _ ,■.
8. “ Righteousness,” P 7? (Tzedek) occurs twelve times, 123, 142 (second), v. 144. 1 7 2 , ren
“ righteous ,” verses 7, 62, 106, 138, 160, 164 ; “ right,'’ verse 75 ; “justice,’ verse 121. Aso e
form npT2 (Tzedakah), verses 40 and 142 (first). It is from pjs, to be right, straight, t en,
upright, just, righteous. Hence, the noun means rightness, straightness, what is right and just.
9. “Statutes,” pn (Chok) occurs twenty-one times (always plural). It is from PPTJ, to xew,
hack, cut in, engrave, inscribe; hence, to decree. “Chok,” therefore, is a decree or oidinance.
10. “Word,” "127 (Davar) occurs twenty-four times (three of them in plural), and is rendere
“Word” or “Words” {viz., verses 9, 16, 17, 25, 28, 42 {twice), 43, 49, 57 {pl-)> 65, 74, 81, 89,
101, 105, 107, 114, 130 (pi.), 139 (pl.), 147, 160, 161, and 169. It is from w, to arrange in a
row, set forth, then to speak. It refers to the utterance, the subject-matter of the revelation, not
to the mode or words by which it is imparted.—(Ed.)

ssalm cxxvii.
A Song of degrees for Solomon.
A | 1 Except the Lord build the house, they labour in vain that build it:
B except the Lord keep the city, the watchman waketh hut in vain.

A \ 3 Lo, children are an heritage of the Lord: and the fruit of the womb is his
j reward.
C | 4 As arrows are in the hand of a mighty man;

D | they shall not be ashamed, but they shall speak with the enemies in the gate.

The second and third members, B and B, may be thus arranged:—(Ed.)
B a | except the Lord keep the city,
b | the watchman waketh but in vain.
B h j 2 It is vain for you to rise up early, to sit up late, to eat the bread of sorrows:
a J for 1 so 2 he giveth his beloved sleep. 3
The Skeleton of B and B.
B | a | -i-. The Lord our Watcher. (iaur)
I b | -1. Vain watching, (loim)
B [ b | 2-. Yain watching.
I a J -2. The Lord our Watcher.
1 Omit “/or.” 2 p “ Thus ,” leferring to what follows.
3 Remembering that the Heb. tom is an adverbial accusative, “ sleeping,” or “in sleep,” the
contrast comes out clearly:— “Thus He (who neither slumbers nor sleeps cxxi. 4) giveth to His
beloved—while they sleep'' Teaching us that others, with all their toil and watching, are not His
beloved, and therefore all their labour is in vain.
The word beloved, i'i* ( Yedid ), is the name given by God to Solomon (Yedidiah), “ beloved of
the Lord " (see 2 Sam. xii. 25). The word “ beloved " here is in the singular, “ his beloved one."
This is the central Psalm of the fifteen “ Songs of degrees ”: the one round which the others
are grouped—seven on either side. It is inscribed “ for Solomon”: and Solomon knew, by personal
experience, how God gave to him abundance of blessings, “ thus—even in sleep (1 Kings iii. 5 —15).
So God gives now to “His beloved.” Thus He gave to Adam (Gen. ii. 21, 22) a bride ; to
Abraham (Gen. xv. 12 —16) a seed innumerable, and builds up His spiritual house to all
generations.- (I'd.)

F 1 -15. Happy People. [True estimate.]
The three-fold division may be arranged thus (Ed.): —
1 I—ll.1 —11. Praise and prayer for deliverance from “ strange children.”
2 12 —14. Their vain speech and falsehood.
3 15. The false and true conclusions.
1 Man who is. 2 ! instead of : and 3 omit “ore.” ....
‘linn, translated “That,” at beginning of v. 12, is “Who.” The figure of ellipsis requires
the addition of the word say from vv. 8 and -n. Thus: “ Who say," vainly and falsely, that
happiness consists in outward and material prosperity. This is the vanity which their mouth
speaketh, while the Divine conclusion is nay, not “yea,” but “ Yea, rather, happy is that people
whose God is the Lord.” The large number of words in italics in vv. 12 14 shows that the
Translators experienced difficulty. But the figure of ellipsis, taken with the structure, . throw the
vain statements of the “ strange children” and their false conclusion in v. 15 into vivid, contrast
with the great truth of the Scriptural definition as to that in which true happiness consists. See
Ps, iv. 6, 7 ; cxlvi. 5, &c.— (Ed.)

Psalm cxlv. is one of the acrostic Psalms, in which each verse begins with the successive letter
of the Hebrew alphabet. It will, however, be seen that there are only twenty-one verses instead
of twenty-two, the fourteenth letter {Nun, 1) having through human infirmity dropped out of the
manuscripts. The verse is, however, preserved in the ancient versions of the Septuagint, Syriac,
Arabic and Ethiopic, and in one manuscript. It begins with the letter i, and reads thus:—“ The
Lord is faithful in all His words, and holy in all His works.” Here the structure comes to the
aid of textual criticism, and proves the propriety of inserting it, for in B 3 this verse (i) makes
the beginning of h correspond with the beginning of h, verse 17. — (Ed.)
1 Shall bless, 3-12*, as in v. 10, all flesh shall bless.”

The Structure of the Book of Psalms as a whole.
TF the structure of each Psalm is perfect in itself, we may well expect to find the
same perfection in the arrangement of the one hundred and fifty Psalms as a whole.
Many attempts have been made from ancient times to discover this structure, and to
classify the Psalms ; but none of them is so satisfactory as to preclude another attempt.
It is certain that the present order in which we have the Psalms is the same as it
was when they were in the hands of our Lord, and were quoted repeatedly by Him,
and by the Holy Spirit through the Evangelists and Apostles. Indeed, in Acts xiii. 33,
the Holy Spirit by Paul expressly mentions “the second Psalm.” This puts us upon
sure ground.
There must be a reason therefore why “the second Psalm” is not, for example, the
seventy-second; and why the ninetieth (which is the most ancient of all the Psalms,
being a prayer of Moses) is not the first. Leaving the unsatisfactory ground of the
conjectures and theories of man (which are incapable of real proof), and confining
ourselves to internal evidence and Manuscript and Massoretic authority, we find that
in the Hebrew text, as we have it to-day, as well as in the ancient versions of it
(including the Septuagint, made more than 200 years 8.C.), the whole collection is
divided into Five Books, as follows :
Book I.—Psalms i.—xli., concluding with a Blessing and “Amen and Amen.”
Book ll.—Psalms xlii. —Ixxii., concluding with a double Blessing and “Amen and
Amen.”
Book 111. —Psalms Ixxiii.—lxxxix., concluding with a Blessing and “Amen and Amen.”
Book IV. —Psalms xc. —cvi., concluding with a Blessing and “Amen, Hallelujah.”
Book V. —Psalms evii.—cl., concluding with “Hallelujah.”
There are in all, seven “Amens” and twenty-four “Hallelujahs,” All the latter
are in Book V. except four, which are in Book IV.
The Midrash on Psalm i. 1, says:—“ Moses gave to the Israelites the five books of
the Law; and, corresponding to these, David gave them the five books of the Psalms.”
Here we have our very word “correspondence”; and our object is to trace it out, and
exhibit it to the eye, so that the Book of Psalms as a whole may be seen to have the
same perfection of structure as each of its individual Psalms.
Book I. (Psalms i.—xli.) is the GENESis-Book.
Book 11. (Psalms xlii. —Ixxii.) is the ExODUS-Book.
Book 111. (Psalms Ixxiii.—lxxxix.) is the LEVmcus-Book.
Book IV. (Psalms xc. —cvi.) is the NuMBERS-Book.
Book V. (Psalms evii.—cl.) is the DEUTERONOMY-Book.
To understand these five Psalm-Books, we must ascertain the distinctive character
of the Pentateuch-Books. This can be learnt, not from the names which man has


given to these hooks (in the Septnagint and Latin Vulgate), hut only from the names
which God has given to them in the Hebrew Canon. We shall find that while man’s
names and titles have been given on account of what he conceived to he the principal
events recorded in the hooks, God’s name points us to what is the real design and great
central commanding thought in the hooks. According to this we shall learn that
Genesis is the hook of the Beginning.
Exodus is the hook of Redemption.
Leviticus is the hook of The Sanctuary.
Numbers is the hook of The Wilderness.
Deuteronomy is the hook of The Law.
The five Psalm-Books correspond to these five Pentateuch-Books. The teaching
of each book is dispensational; i.e., it is teaching concerning the Counsels and Pur-
poses of God, past, present, and future ; and each Psalm-Book views these Counsels
and Purposes in their relation to the special character of the Pentateuch-Book. The
first Psalm in each Book is the key-note and epitome of the whole.
BOOK I— (PSALMS I.—XLL)— THE GENESIS-BOOK.
GENESIS is the Greek yeWis ( generation ), and is the name given to the hook
by the Septnagint translators, as descriptive of its subject-matter.
The Divine name for it is nwm “In the Beginning.” It is the hook of the
beginning : and in it we read of the beginning of the Earth, of Life, of Man, and of
Israel. It is the “seed-plot” of the whole Bible. Like the trees of Gen. i. 11, 12, its
“ seed is in itself.” It contains, in germ, type and prophecy, the essence of Divine
Revelation. It tells of the beginning of Life, and its types are the lives of indi-
vidual men.*
In the first Book of the Psalms we find that the leading thought corresponds with
that of the first hook of the Pentateuch. The purposes and counsels of God are
shown from the beginning to the end in relation to MAN. As Genesis begins with
the Divine blessing on Man (i. 28), so Psalm i. opens with “ Blessed is the man."
All blessedness for man is shown to consist in subjection to, and occupation
with, God’s Law. It is the Tree of Life to him: and, meditating on this, he becomes
like a well-watered tree in the Paradise of God. But in Gen. iii. Man rebelled against
that Law: and Ps. ii. describes the consequences of this rebellion, while Ps. iii. takes
its title from one who rebelled against God’s King. The Ruin can be repaired only
by THE MAN, Christ Jesus (“the Seed of the woman”): and in the Psalms of this
first Book (the second section) we see Him in His Atoning Work, which alone sets
man again in the blessedness which he has lost.
The first Book consists of forty-one Psalms. The central Psalm is xxi., which sets
forth the eternal life aud blessedness of God’s King. All that have titles (37) are
David’s —the man of God’s choice. The four without titles (i., ii., x. and xxsiii.) are
*So with the other Books. The types in Exodus are types of Redemption ; the types in
Leviticus are types of the Sanctuary ; while the types in Numbers are types of the Wilderness.


also probably David’s; for Ps. i. and ii. are David’s,* while x. and xxxiii. each follow
one by David, and, according to an ancient rule of interpretation, would be reckoned
as David’s.
Of the Divine Titles, Jehovah occurs 279 times, and Elohim only 48 times (9 of
which are joined with Jehovah). Note also the references to the events, &c., of Genesis
in this first Book.

BOOK II. —(PSALMS XLII. —LXXII.) — THE EXODUS-BOOK.
EXODUS is the Greek e£oSos, and is the name given to the hook by the Septnagint
Translators as descriptive of its chief event —the going out of the Children of Israel
from Egypt. But the Bible title for it is nintp n.'wq, “And these are the names.’
The Book is thus called because it begins with the names of those who came into
the place whence they were redeemed and delivered from their ruined condition.*
Exodus is therefore the Book of Redemption : and Redemption is individual and
by name. It is the Book in which the Redemption of the People is first mentioned:
“ Thou in Thy mercy hast led forth the people which Thou hast Redeemed ; Thou
hast guided them in Thy strength unto Thy holy habitation.” (Exodus xv. 13). The
types of Exodus are also types of Redemption. The Divine title JAH (Hj), the
concentrated form of Jehovah, occurs for the first time in the book of Exodus (xv. 3) ;
and it also occurs for the first time in the Psalms in this second or Exodus-Book
(Psalm Ixviii. 4).
In this second book of the Psalms we find the subject-matter corresponding to
Exodus. Like the other books, its teaching is dispensational. In the Genesis-Book, Man
is the central thought; in this Exodus-Book, it is the XATIOX OP ISRAEL around
which the counsels and purposes of God are centred. It opens with the “ cry from
the depth of the Ruin, as Exodus does; and it ends with the Kiug reigning over the
redeemed nation (Ps. Ixxii.), brought “ again the second time from the four coincis
of the earth (Isaiah xi. 11); as it was brought the first time from Egypt; and made a
blessing to all the families of the earth.
Of the Divine names and titles : Elohim occurs 262 times (two of them with
Jehovah), El, 14 times, and Jehovah only 37 times. Xote the references to Sinai,
Miriam, and other events in Exodus in this second book.
It consists of thirty-one Psalms, divided into three parts, arranged as follows
(1) The first (xlii.— xlix.) concerning Israel’s Ruin (all Psalms for the Sons
of Korah, who escaped the Ruin of their Father in the wilderness;
Num. xxvi. 11).
(2) The second (1. —lx.) concerning Israel’s Redeemer.
(3) The third (Ixi. —Ixxii.) concerning Israel’s Redemption.
# There is more, however, than this. Not only does the Lord speak so pointedly of knowing
Moses “by name” (xxxiii. 12, 17), but Moses asks by what Name he is to speak of the God of
their fathers, to the Israelites (hi. 13), and the Lord reveals His Name (hi. 14, 15), while in vi. 3,

concerning the Name of the Lord (xx. 7). Bezaleel is said to have been “called” by name
(xxxi. 2), whereas a different phrase is used of Aholiab (xxxi. 6) both here and in xxxv. 30 and 34.
It is in Exodus also that we have the particular instructions as to the engraving of the names on
the shoulder-stones of the Ephod (xxviii. 9—12), and on the Breast-plate stones (15—21), which
were strictly carried out (xxxix. 6, 7 and 8 — 14). Thus “ the names of the children of Isiael
were borne before the Lord with the Redeeming Blood in the Holy of Holies. So that these names
appear at the beginning of Exodus, in connection with the Ruin ; and at the end in connection
with the Redemption “ before God in the Sanctuary ” ; while we have the Name of the Redeemer
proclaimed and celebrated throughout, “The Lord is His Name” (Ex. xv. 3).

BOOK lII— (PSALMS LXXIIL—LXXXIX.)— THE LEVITICUS-BOOK.
LEVITICUS is, again, the title which man has given to this Book to indicate its
subject-matter, viz., the ordinances, &c., pertaining to the Levites. The title in the
Hebrew Canon is “ And he called.” It is the Book of the SANCTUARY. It tells
how God is to he approached, and teaches ns that none can worship except such as are
called, and whom “ the Father seeks to worship Him.” Hence it is written,“Blessed
is the man whom Thou choosest, and causest to approach unto Thee , that he may
dwell in Thy courts; we shall be satisfied with the goodness of Thy house, even of Thy
holy temple.’ The types in this hook are types of the Sanctuary, i.e., of Access and
Worship.
In this Leviticus-Book of the Psalms we find the corresponding thought. Its
teaching is dispensational as in the other books ; but in this the counsels of God are
seen, not in relation to Man , not in relation to the Nation, but in relation to the
SANCTUARY, which is mentioned or referred to in nearly every Psalm of this Book.
The Sanctuary is seen from its ruin to its establishment in the fulness of blessing.
The Book consists of only seventeen Psalms, which are divided into two sections:—
(1) The first (Psalm Ixxiii. —Ixxxiii.) the Sanctuary in its relation to Man.
(2) The second (Psalms Ixxxiv. —Ixxxix.) the Sanctuary in relation to Jehovah.
Consequently in theirs/, which is composed wholly of “Asaph” Psalms, Elohim
is mentioned 65 times (two of them with Jehovah), and Jehovah only 15 times; while
in the second (composed of 4 Korah, 1 David, and 1 Ethan), Jehovah is mentioned 50
times, and Elohim only 28 times (4 of which are joined to Jehovah) ; El, 5 times.
(r) THE SANCTUARY IN ITS RELATION TO MAN.
A Ixxiii. (Asaph). The effect of being away from the Sanctuary. Occupation of
heart with others, and consequent distraction.

whole of this Book,
BOOK IV. —(PSALMS XC.—CYI.)— THE NUMBERS-BOOK.
NUMBERS is again the name that man has given to the fourth book of the
Pentateuch, on account of the numberings recorded in chapters i. iii. and xxvi. It is
from the Latin Vulgate. The title in the Hebrew Canon is 15703, Le., In ihe
Wilderness.” This title covers all the events recorded in this Book. “Numbers,
therefore, is the Book of the WILDERNESS, and its types are wilderness types, or
types of our pilgrimage.
In the Numbers-Book of the Psalms we find the corresponding subject. It opens
with Psalm xc., “ A prayer of Moses,” —the man of the wilderness ! Its teaching, like
that of the other Books, is dispensational, with the EARTH as its central thought.
God’s Counsels and Purposes are celebrated with regard to the Earth, and the Nations
of the Earth, from the Ruin to the Glory; as in the other Books we have seen
them set forth with regard to (1) Man, (2) Israel, and (3) the Sanctuary.
Sin has come into the world, and ruined not merely Man, but the Earth itself :
“ Cursed is the ground for thy sake.” Sin has made the paradise of God a wilderness,
and death has filled it with sorrow and sadness. There is no hope for the Earth, and
no hope for the Nations of the Earth apart from Jehovah. The first and second
Psalms (xc. and xci.) set this forth, and give, as it were, the key-note and epitome of
the whole Book. Its figures are from this wilderness-world; as mountains, hills,
floods, grass, pestilence, trees, &c., &c., which the reader will notice for himself.
Happiness for the world will be found only when He “ whose right it is shall come
again to reign and “judge the world in righteousness.” In Christ, the coming King,
not only Israel, but all the nations of the earth will be blessed. This is the theme of
the Book. (See note on Psalm xcvi. 11.)
It consists, like Book 111., of seventeen Psalms, all of which are anonymous
(though not all without titles) except xc. (and xci.*), Moses’s, and ci., ciii., which are
David’s.
* If xci. be a Psalm of Moses (following Psalm xc.) then all the Scriptures quote d in our Lord’s
Temptation (even that which the evil one tried to quote) were from the writings of Moses!


Jehovah occurs 126 times, and Elohim 31 (10 of which are with Jehovah) ; El,
six times.
It is divided into three sections, as follows: —
(1) The first, Psalms xc. —xciv. Rest for the Earth desired. No hope for
the Earth till “ the wicked cease from troubling, and the weary are at
rest.”
(2) The second , Psalms xcv. —c. Rest for the Earth anticipated. “ Let the
heavens rejoice and let the earth be glad.” “ For He cometh to judge
the earth” (see xcvi. 11, note, page 92).
(3) The third, Psalms ci.—cvi. Rest for the Earth enjoyed. “ The Lord
hath prepared His throne in the heavens: and His kingdom ruleth over
all” (ciii. 19).
(1) REST FOR THE EARTH DESIRED.
A xc., xci. (Moses). Jehovah the only abiding place in a perishing world: and the
secret place of the Most High the only place of safety in it.
B xcii. The Sabbath day the only Rest in a wicked world, telling of that Sab-
bath-keeping to come, when the “workers of iniquity” shall be cut off ( v . 7,9,
11) and the righteous shall flourish (r. 12) in Jehovah their Rock and defence

BOOK V. — (PSALMS CVIL— CL.)—THE DEUTERONOMY-BOOK.
DEUTERONOMY is, again, Man’s name for this Book. It is from the Greek
Septuagint, and means “the second Law.” Itw T as given because Deuteronomy was a
repetition of the Law to the new generation. The title in the Hebrew' canon is oyyin nV«,
“These are the Words.” It is the Book which contains the words of God, and
almost wholly consists of the testimonies, statutes, and judgments, &c., of Jehovah. It
was from this Book that the Saviour made His three quotations, when He met the
tempter with the three-fold “It is written.” It follows the Book of the Wilderness,
and gives the reason for all the trials of their pilgrimage: —“ The Lord thy God led
thee these forty years . . . that He might make thee know that man doth not live hy
bread only, but by every word that proceedeth out of the mouth of the Lord doth man
live.” (Dent. viii. 2,3.) The natural life, the giving of which is recorded in Genesis,
is nothing worth if man is not begotten hy the Word, and if the new natui'e thus given
is not nourished by the Word. Eor only thus can man he truly said to live.
Hence, in this Deuteronomy-Book of the Psalms we have the same leading subject.
Its teaching is like that of the other Books, dispensational; and it is grouped around the
WORD. All blessing for Man (Book i.), all blessing for Israel (Book ii.), all blessing
for Zion (Book iii.), all blessing for the Earth and its Nations (Book iv.), is bound up
in the Word and Law of God. The breaking of that Law had been the source of Man’s
sorrow, Israel’s dispersion, the Temple’s ruin, and Earth’s misery. It will yet be seen
that all blessing for Man, the gathering of Israel, the building of Zion, and restoration
for the Earth, is bound up with the Word of God, and with His Laws written by His
Spirit on the fleshy tables of the heart.
What a wonderful thing for one to be brought to say “Oh how I love Thy Law! ”
(Psalm cxix. 97*), when the breaking of that Law had brought in all the suffering }
But it will be noted that this is said only after (in Psalm cxviii.) the Resurrection
of the Righteous Magnifier of that Law has been celebrated.
This is the Theme of the Deuteronomy-Book of the Psalms. It consists of forty-four
Psalms, in which the title of Jehovah occurs 293 times; and Jah, 13 ; while Elohim
occurs only 41 times (4 of which are with Jehovah) ; El, 10 times; Eloha, twice.
While the structure of the other Books consists of two or three sections, this Book
is, like the Law of God itself, a perfect whole. It is the only Book which has an even
number of Psalms. Its first Psalm (cvii.), as is the case with the first Psalms of the
other Books, is at once its key-note and epitome.
*lt will be noted that the characteristic Psalm cxix. occurs in this book; as Ixxxiv. does in the
Leviticus-Book; and xc. in the Numbers-Book, &c.

A KEY TO THE PSALMS.
The Hev. Dr. Bellinger has much pleasure in announcing that a new and
S “ B °° k ° f PBalmS “ n ° W b6ing Pr “ ted ’ ” d will be
Its object is to exhibit to the eye each Psalm, so printed as to display at one view
6 P r e ‘ £eCtlon ° f lts plan ’ the symmetry of its structure, and the point of its teaching.
1 here is a principle of construction which prevails in the Old and New Testa-
ments !on g recognised by Biblical scholars, and called “ parallelism ”; bnt this had
hitherto been noticed only in verses and short passages. It was reserved for the late
Rev. Thomas Boys to show that the same principle (which he terms “correspondence ”)
extends to whole chapters and even Books, and is not confined to those parts which
have been called “ Poetical,” but is found also to pervade the Historical and
Epistolary portions of the Word of God. In 1824 Mr. Boys published his Tactica
Sacra, m which he exhibited the structure of several of the Epistles; and in 1825 he
published his Key to the Booh of Psalms , in which he explained the whole subject, and
gave examples of sixteen of the Psalms which he had at that time arranged.
At Ins death, in 1880, he left certain materials, which have since been placed in the
lands of Dr. Bullmger, and have enabled him to arrange the whole of the Psalms,
and to issue them in a complete form.
I rom the specimen of one given herewith (Psalm cv.) it will be seen that it is
not a mere plan made for the Psalm; but that the plan is exhibited on which the
Psalm m actually constructed, showing that the words “ which the Holy Ghost
teacheth ” are not written with the imperfection which pertains to man’s writings,
but with an order, method, perfection and precision peculiar to themselves, and not
found in any mere human composition. The great central thought of each Psalm,
and the object of its teaching, is thus discovered and clearly brought out. A reference
to “the skeleton ” of this Psalm will explain the use of the letters employed, and show
how the subject of one member of it (marked by a Roman letter) corresponds with that
of the other (marked by an italic letter).
The work will consist of a Preface by the Rev. Sydney Thelwall, 8.A., Vicar
of Westleigh, North Devon, through whom, in God’s providence, Mr. Boys’s papers
have been preserved; and an Introduction by the Editor, giving a full explanation of
the principles and their application, which is necessary for a due understanding and
appreciation of the work; these will be followed by each Psalm in order, with its
“Skeleton” or Key, and such brief notes connected with its structure as may be
required; the work concluding with an Appendix, by the Editor, on the Psalms as a whole ,
showing that each Psalm is only a member of some larger arrangement, and exhibiting
the plan on which the one hundred and fifty Psalms are arranged (in their Books,
divisions, sections, &c.). The mutual relation of each Psalm will thus be set forth, ’
and the reason why it occupies the particular place assigned to it.
The lext will be printed from the Authorised Version; and, in the case of the
Divine Titles, the types will be so employed as to secure uniformity, and enable the
reader easily to distinguish each of the Divine Names and Titles: (Jehovah, Jah,
Adon, Adonai, Adonim, El, Elohim, Eloah, Elyon, Shaddai, and Messiah:) which will
all be explained in the Introduction.
1 he price of the wmrk will be Five Shillings , post free, and it will be published by
Di. Bullinger. All orders are to be sent to him, addressed, simply, Woking.
I lepayment is requested in order to save the time, trouble and expense involved in
the keeping of accounts, and in the collection of unpaid subscriptions after publication.
Friends are asked kindly to assist in the circulation of this prospectus among
Bible students. Extra copies of it will be gladly supplied for this purpose.
